       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>12</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-79"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>15</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       General rankings
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> Penn is currently ranked 8th in the United States (tied with <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke)</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Chicago" title="The University of Chicago" class="mw-redirect">The University of Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The eighth position is three spots down compared to 2011; the university attributed the drop in <i>U.S. News'</i> new methodology that takes into account the opinions of high school college counselors, who emphasize the benefits of large urban centers like New York.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>U.S. News</i> also includes Penn in its Most Popular National Universities list,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> and so does <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i> in its Dream Colleges list.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In their latest editions Penn was ranked 12th in the world by the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS&nbsp;World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> 14th by the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWU-85"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and 15th by the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings"><i>Times Higher Education</i> World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-86"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Shanghai Jiao Tong University ranking Penn is also the 8th and 9th best university in the world for economics/business and social sciences studies, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> University of Pennsylvania ranked 12th among 300 Best World Universities in 2012 compiled by <a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a> (HRLR) on Measurements of World's Top 300 Universities Graduates' Performance .<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       Research rankings
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>The Center for Measuring University Performance places Penn in the first tier of the United States' top research universities (tied with <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford" title="Stanford" class="mw-redirect">Stanford</a>), based on research expenditures, faculty awards, PhD granted and other academic criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Penn was also ranked 9th by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> in terms of R&amp;D expenditures topping all other Ivy League Schools.<sup id="cite_ref-nsf.gov_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsf.gov-51"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> research performance index ranks Penn 8th in the world, whereas the 2010 Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities (published by the Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan) ranks Penn 11th in the world for 2010, 2008 and 2007, and 9th for 2009.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers measures universities' research productivity, research impact, and research excellence based on the scientific papers published by their academic staff. The <a href="/wiki/SCImago_Journal_Rank" title="SCImago Journal Rank">SCImago</a> Institutions Rankings World Report 2012, which ranks world universities, national institutions and academies in terms of research output, ranks Penn 7th nationally among U.S. universities (and 2nd in the Ivy League behind Harvard) and 28th in the world overall (the first being France's <a href="/wiki/French_National_Centre_for_Scientific_Research" title="French National Centre for Scientific Research">Centre National de la Recherche Scientifique</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       Other rankings
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mines_ParisTech" title="Mines ParisTech">Mines ParisTech</a> International Professional Ranking, which ranks universities on the basis of the number of alumni listed among CEOs in the 500 largest worldwide companies, ranks Penn 11th worldwide, and 2nd nationally behind Harvard.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a <i>US News</i> article in 2010, Penn is tied for second (tied with <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts University</a>) for the number of undergraduate alumni who are current Fortune 100 CEOs.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Monthly" title="The Washington Monthly" class="mw-redirect">The Washington Monthly</a></i> ranked Penn 27th in National University Rankings (Social mobility: percentage of, and support for, Pell grant recipients; Research: total research spending; PhDs granted in science and engineering; and Community Service: the number of students in ROTC, Peace Corps, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> ranked Penn 17th, based on a variety of criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       Undergraduate programs
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Penn's arts and science programs are all well regarded, with many departments ranked amongst the nation's top 10. At the undergraduate level, <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">Wharton</a>, Penn's business school, and Penn's nursing school have maintained their No. 1, 2 or 3 rankings since <i>U.S. News</i> began reviewing such programs.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the School of Engineering, top departments are <a href="/wiki/Bioengineering" title="Bioengineering" class="mw-redirect">bioengineering</a> (typically ranked in the top 5 by <i>U.S. News</i>), <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The school is also strong in some areas of computer science and <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>.</p> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       Graduate and professional programs
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Among its professional schools, the schools of <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annenberg_School_for_Communication_at_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Annenberg School for Communication at the University of Pennsylvania">communication</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="University of Pennsylvania School of Dental Medicine">dentistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perelman_School_of_Medicine_at_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Perelman School of Medicine at the University of Pennsylvania">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_School_of_Nursing" title="University of Pennsylvania School of Nursing">nursing</a>, and veterinary medicine rank in the top 5 nationally (see <i>U.S. News</i> and National Research Council).<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Penn's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_Law_School" title="University of Pennsylvania Law School">Law School</a> is ranked 7th, and its <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania_Graduate_School_of_Education" title="University of Pennsylvania Graduate School of Education">School of Education</a> and School of Social Policy &amp; Practice are ranked in the top 10 (see <i>U.S. News</i>).<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the 2010 <a href="/wiki/QS_Global_200_Business_Schools_Report" title="QS Global 200 Business Schools Report">QS Global 200 Business Schools Report</a>, Penn was ranked 2nd in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <dl> 
      <dt>
       Executive salary
      </dt> 
     </dl> 
     <p>Amy Gutmann's salary in 2009 was <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.3 million</span>, placing her as the 20th highest paid college president in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-pbjstaff2011_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbjstaff2011-96"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-phillips2011_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phillips2011-97"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Of those accepted for admission to the Class of 2014, 40.8 percent are <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>, African-American, or <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Penn:_Penn_Facts_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penn:_Penn_Facts-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, 51.1% of current students are women.<sup id="cite_ref-Penn:_Penn_Facts_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penn:_Penn_Facts-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>More than 11% of the first year class are <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">international students</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Penn:_Penn_Facts_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penn:_Penn_Facts-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The composition of international students accepted in the Class of 2014 is: 50.2% from Asia; 9.2% from Africa and the Middle East; 17.7% from Europe; 15.5% from Canada and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>; 4.8% from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, Central America, and South America; 1.1% from Australia and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Penn:_Penn_Facts_3-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penn:_Penn_Facts-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The acceptance rate for international students applying for the class of 2014 was 411 out of 4,390 (9.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-Penn:_Penn_Facts_3-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penn:_Penn_Facts-3"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_student_organizations">Selected student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Selected student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Philomathean_Society" title="Philomathean Society">Philomathean Society</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Philomathean_Society" title="Philomathean Society">Philomathean Society</a>, founded in 1813,<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_Philomathean_society_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_Philomathean_society-99"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> is the United States' oldest continuously existing collegiate literary society. The <a href="/wiki/Mask_and_Wig" title="Mask and Wig">Mask and Wig Club</a> is the oldest all-male musical comedy troupe in the country. <a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Pennsylvania_Glee_Club" title="The University of Pennsylvania Glee Club" class="mw-redirect">The University of Pennsylvania Glee Club</a>, founded in 1862, is one of the oldest continually operating collegiate choruses in the United States. <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Montgomery_(entertainer)" title="Bruce Montgomery (entertainer)">Bruce Montgomery</a>, its best-known and longest-serving director, led the club from 1956 until 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Montgomery_Obituary_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery_Obituary-100"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The International Affairs Association (IAA) was founded in 1963 as an organization to promote international affairs and diplomacy at Penn and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> With over 400 members, it is the largest student-funded organization on campus. The IAA serves as an umbrella organization for various conferences (<a href="/w/index.php?title=UPMUNC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UPMUNC (page does not exist)">UPMUNC</a>, ILMUNC, and PIRC), as well as a host of other academic and social activities.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Pennsylvania_Band" title="The University of Pennsylvania Band">The University of Pennsylvania Band</a> has been a part of student life since 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-Who_are_we.3F.21_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who_are_we.3F.21-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The Penn Band performs at football and basketball games as well as university functions (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>) throughout the year and was the first college band to perform at <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade">Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Who_are_we.3F.21_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who_are_we.3F.21-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Membership fluctuates between 80 and 100 students.<sup id="cite_ref-Who_are_we.3F.21_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who_are_we.3F.21-102"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Daily_Pennsylvanian"><i>The Daily Pennsylvanian</i></span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The Daily Pennsylvanian">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Pennsylvanian" title="The Daily Pennsylvanian">The Daily Pennsylvanian</a>
     </div> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Pennsylvanian" title="The Daily Pennsylvanian">The Daily Pennsylvanian</a></i> is an independent, student-run newspaper, which has been published daily since it was founded in 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The newspaper went unpublished from May 1943 to November 1945 due to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1984, the University lost all editorial and financial control of <i>The Daily Pennsylvanian</i> when the newspaper became its own corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_The_Daily_Pennsylvanian-103"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, <i>The Daily Pennsylvanian</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Pacemaker_Award" title="Pacemaker Award" class="mw-redirect">Pacemaker Award</a> administered by the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Collegiate_Press" title="Associated Collegiate Press">Associated Collegiate Press</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Penn_Quakers" title="Penn Quakers">Penn Quakers</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Penn's <a href="/wiki/College_athletics" title="College athletics">sports</a> teams are nicknamed the <a href="/wiki/Religious_Society_of_Friends" title="Religious Society of Friends" class="mw-redirect">Quakers</a>. They participate in the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> (Division I FCS for football) in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. In recent decades they often have been <a href="/wiki/Sports_league" title="Sports league">league</a> champions in football (14 times from 1982 to 2010) and basketball (22 times from 1970 to 2006). The first athletic team at Penn was its <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> team.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rowing">Rowing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rowing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">Rowing</a> at Penn dates back to at least 1854 with the founding of the <a href="/wiki/University_Barge_Club" title="University Barge Club">University Barge Club</a>. The university currently hosts both heavyweight and lightweight men's teams and an openweight women's team, all of which compete as part of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Sprints" title="Eastern Sprints">Eastern Sprints</a> League. Penn Rowing has produced a long list of famous coaches and Olympians, including <a href="/wiki/Susan_Francia" title="Susan Francia">Susan Francia</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_B._Kelly,_Jr." title="John B. Kelly, Jr.">John B. Kelly, Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Burk" title="Joe Burk">Joe Burk</a>, Rusty Callow, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Parker_(rower)" title="Harry Parker (rower)">Harry Parker</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Nash_(rower)" title="Ted Nash (rower)">Ted Nash</a>. The teams row out of <a href="/wiki/College_Boat_Club" title="College Boat Club">College Boat Club</a>, No.&nbsp;11 <a href="/wiki/Boathouse_Row" title="Boathouse Row">Boathouse Row</a>. The program is currently under the direction of men's head coach Greg Myhr.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby">Rugby</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rugby">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Penn Men's <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby</a> Football Club is recognized as one of the oldest collegiate rugby teams in America. The earliest documentation of its existence comes from a 1910 issue of the <i>Daily Pennsylvanian.</i> The team existed on and off during the <a href="/wiki/World_War" title="World War" class="mw-redirect">World Wars</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:File_Upload_Wizard?wpDestFile=Penn_Park.jpg" class="new" title="File:Penn Park.jpg">File:Penn Park.jpg</a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        The newly-built state of the art sports complex at the University of Pennsylvania.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The current club has its roots in the 1960s. The University of Pennsylvania rugby teams play in the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Rugby_Conference" title="Ivy Rugby Conference">Ivy Rugby Conference</a>, and have finished as runners-up in both 15s and 7s.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2011, the club now utilize the state-of-the-art facilities at <a href="/wiki/Penn_Park" title="Penn Park">Penn Park</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.upennrugby.com/">Quakers Rugby</a> played on national TV at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Rugby_Championship" title="Collegiate Rugby Championship">Collegiate Rugby Championship</a>, a college rugby tournament played every June at <a href="/wiki/PPL_Park" title="PPL Park">PPL Park</a> in Philadelphia and broadcast live on NBC. In their inaugural year of participation, the Penn Men's rugby team won the Shield Competition, beating local rivals <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.temple.edu/studentaffairs/campusrec/programs/sportclubs/rugby-men.asp?">Temple University</a> 17-12 in the final. In doing so, they became the first Philadelphia team to beat a non-Philadelphia team in CRC history, with a 14-12 win over the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.utrugby.com/">University of Texas</a> in the Shield semi-final.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:FranklinFieldPenn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/FranklinFieldPenn.jpg/220px-FranklinFieldPenn.jpg" width="220" height="86" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/FranklinFieldPenn.jpg/330px-FranklinFieldPenn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/FranklinFieldPenn.jpg/440px-FranklinFieldPenn.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:FranklinFieldPenn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Field" title="Franklin Field">Franklin Field</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Penn first fielded a <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team against <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Germantown_Cricket_Club" title="Germantown Cricket Club">Germantown Cricket Club</a> in Philadelphia on November 11, 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-Fight_song_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fight_song-108"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Penn football made many contributions to the sport in its early days. During the 1890s, Penn's famed coach and alumnus <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_Woodruff" title="George Washington Woodruff">George Washington Woodruff</a> introduced the quarterback kick, a forerunner of the <a href="/wiki/Forward_pass" title="Forward pass">forward pass</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Placekicker" title="Placekicker">place-kick</a> from scrimmage and the delayed pass. In 1894, 1895, 1897, and 1904, Penn was generally regarded as the national champion of collegiate football.<sup id="cite_ref-Fight_song_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fight_song-108"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> The achievements of two of Penn's outstanding players from that era?<a href="/wiki/John_Heisman" title="John Heisman">John Heisman</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Outland" title="John Outland" class="mw-redirect">John Outland</a>?are remembered each year with the presentation of the <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> to the most outstanding college football player of the year, and the <a href="/wiki/Outland_Trophy" title="Outland Trophy">Outland Trophy</a> to the most outstanding college football <a href="/wiki/Lineman_(American_football)" title="Lineman (American football)">interior lineman</a> of the year.</p> 
     <p>In addition, each year the <a href="/wiki/Bednarik_Award" title="Bednarik Award" class="mw-redirect">Bednarik Award</a> is given to college football's best defensive player. <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Bednarik" title="Chuck Bednarik">Chuck Bednarik</a> (Class of 1949) was a three-time <a href="/wiki/All-America" title="All-America">All-American</a> <a href="/wiki/Center_(American_football)" title="Center (American football)" class="mw-redirect">center</a>/<a href="/wiki/Linebacker" title="Linebacker">linebacker</a> who starred on the 1947 team and is generally regarded as Penn's all-time finest. In addition to Bednarik, the '47 squad boasted four-time All-American <a href="/wiki/Offensive_tackle" title="Offensive tackle" class="mw-redirect">tackle</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Savitsky" title="George Savitsky">George Savitsky</a> and three-time All-American <a href="/wiki/Halfback_(American_football)" title="Halfback (American football)">halfback</a> <a href="/wiki/Skip_Minisi" title="Skip Minisi">Skip Minisi</a>. All three standouts were subsequently elected to the <a href="/wiki/College_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="College Football Hall of Fame">College Football Hall of Fame</a>, as was their coach, <a href="/wiki/George_Munger_(American_football)" title="George Munger (American football)">George Munger</a> (a star running back at Penn in the early '30s). Bednarik went on to play for 12 years with the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a>, becoming the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL's</a> last 60-minute man. He was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> in 1969. During his presidency of the institution from 1948 to 1953, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Stassen" title="Harold Stassen">Harold Stassen</a> attempted to recultivate Penn's heyday of big-time <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a>, but the effort lacked support and was short-lived.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/College_GameDay_(football)" title="College GameDay (football)">College GameDay</a></i> traveled to Penn to highlight the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>-Penn game on November 17, 2002, the first time the popular college football show had visited an Ivy League campus.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_Palestra.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_Palestra.JPG/220px-The_Palestra.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_Palestra.JPG/330px-The_Palestra.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/The_Palestra.JPG/440px-The_Palestra.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_Palestra.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Palestra" title="Palestra">Palestra</a>, &quot;Cathedral of Basketball&quot;
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Penn_Quakers_men%27s_basketball" title="Penn Quakers men's basketball">Penn Quakers men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Penn <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> is steeped in tradition. Penn made its only (and the Ivy League's second) <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> appearance in 1979, where the Quakers lost to <a href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson" title="Magic Johnson">Magic Johnson</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans" title="Michigan State Spartans">Michigan State</a> in Salt Lake City. (Dartmouth twice finished second in the tournament in the 1940s, but that was before the beginning of formal League play.) Penn's team is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Big_5" title="Philadelphia Big 5">Philadelphia Big 5</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/La_Salle_University" title="La Salle University">La Salle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph%27s_University" title="Saint Joseph's University">Saint Joseph's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Villanova_University" title="Villanova University">Villanova</a>. In 2007, the men's team won its third consecutive Ivy League title and then lost in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a> to <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_Aggies" title="Texas A&amp;M Aggies">Texas A&amp;M</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Franklin_Field" title="Franklin Field">Franklin Field</a> is where the Quakers play football, <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sprint_football" title="Sprint football">sprint football</a>, and track and field (and formerly soccer). It is the oldest stadium still operating for football games and was the first stadium to sport two tiers. It hosted the first commercially televised football game, was once the home field of the Philadelphia Eagles, and was the site of early <a href="/wiki/Army%E2%80%93Navy_Game" title="Army?Navy Game">Army ? Navy</a> games. Today it is also used by Penn students for recreation such as <a href="/wiki/Intramural_sports" title="Intramural sports">intramural</a> and club sports, including <a href="/wiki/Touch_football_(American)" title="Touch football (American)">touch football</a> and cricket. Franklin Field hosts the annual collegiate track and field event &quot;the <a href="/wiki/Penn_Relays" title="Penn Relays">Penn Relays</a>.&quot;</p> 
     <p>Penn's home court, the <a href="/wiki/Palestra" title="Palestra">Palestra</a>, is an arena used for men's and women's basketball teams, volleyball teams, <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a> team, and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Big_5" title="Philadelphia Big 5">Philadelphia Big Five basketball</a>, as well as high school sporting events. The Palestra has hosted more NCAA Tournament basketball games than any other facility. Penn baseball plays its home games at <a href="/wiki/Meiklejohn_Stadium" title="Meiklejohn Stadium">Meiklejohn Stadium</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Boycott_Games" title="Olympic Boycott Games" class="mw-redirect">Olympic Boycott Games</a> of 1980 were held at the University of Pennsylvania in response to Moscow's hosting of the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_war_in_Afghanistan" title="Soviet war in Afghanistan">Soviet incursion in Afghanistan</a>. Twenty-nine of the boycotting nations participated in the Boycott Games.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Pennsylvania_people" title="List of University of Pennsylvania people">List of University of Pennsylvania people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Pennsylvania">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Pennsylvania</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Chomsky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chomsky.jpg/170px-Chomsky.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chomsky.jpg/255px-Chomsky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Chomsky.jpg/340px-Chomsky.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Chomsky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a> studied philosophy and linguistics at Penn graduating with a BA in 1949, an MA in 1951, and a PhD in 1955.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg/170px-William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg" width="170" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg/255px-William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg/340px-William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:William_Carlos_Williams_passport_photograph_1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Physician and poet 
        <a href="/wiki/William_Carlos_Williams" title="William Carlos Williams">William Carlos Williams</a> studied at Penn's School of Medicine.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Penn has produced many alumni that have distinguished themselves in the sciences, academia, politics, the military, arts and media. The size, quality, and diversity of Penn's alumni body has established it as one of the most powerful alumni networks in the United States and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Twelve heads of state or government have attended or graduated from Penn, including former U.S. president <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> former Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> <a href="/wiki/Cesar_Virata" title="Cesar Virata">Cesar Virata</a>; the first president of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nnamdi_Azikiwe" title="Nnamdi Azikiwe">Nnamdi Azikiwe</a>; the first president of <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a>; and the current president of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="C&ocirc;te d'Ivoire" class="mw-redirect">C&ocirc;te d'Ivoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alassane_Ouattara" title="Alassane Ouattara">Alassane Ouattara</a>. Other notable politicians who hold a degree from Penn include former ambassador to China and former 2012 presidential candidate and Utah governor <a href="/wiki/Jon_Huntsman,_Jr." title="Jon Huntsman, Jr.">Jon Huntsman, Jr.</a>, Mexico's current minister of finance, <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_J._Cordero" title="Ernesto J. Cordero" class="mw-redirect">Ernesto J. Cordero</a>, long-serving Pennsylvania senator <a href="/wiki/Arlen_Specter" title="Arlen Specter">Arlen Specter</a>, and former Pennsylvania governor <a href="/wiki/Ed_Rendell" title="Ed Rendell">Ed Rendell</a>.</p> 
     <p>The university's presence in the judiciary in and outside of the United States is also notable. It has produced three <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">United States Supreme Court</a> justices, <a href="/wiki/William_J._Brennan" title="William J. Brennan" class="mw-redirect">William J. Brennan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owen_J._Roberts" title="Owen J. Roberts" class="mw-redirect">Owen J. Roberts</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Wilson" title="James Wilson">James Wilson</a>, Supreme Court justices of foreign states (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Wilson" title="Ronald Wilson">Ronald Wilson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia" title="High Court of Australia">High Court of Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ayala_Procaccia" title="Ayala Procaccia">Ayala Procaccia</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Supreme_Court" title="Israel Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">Israel Supreme Court</a>), <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> judge Nona Tsotsoria, and founders of international law firms (e.g. <a href="/wiki/James_Harry_Covington" title="James Harry Covington">James Harry Covington</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Covington_%26_Burling" title="Covington &amp; Burling">Covington &amp; Burling</a>), <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lipton" title="Martin Lipton">Martin Lipton</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Wachtell,_Lipton,_Rosen,_%26_Katz" title="Wachtell, Lipton, Rosen, &amp; Katz" class="mw-redirect">Wachtell, Lipton, Rosen, &amp; Katz</a>), and <a href="/wiki/George_Wharton_Pepper" title="George Wharton Pepper" class="mw-redirect">George Wharton Pepper</a> (U.S. Senator from Pennsylvania and founder of <a href="/wiki/Pepper_Hamilton" title="Pepper Hamilton">Pepper Hamilton</a>).</p> 
     <p>Penn alumni also have a strong presence in financial and economic life. Penn has educated several governors of central banks including <a href="/wiki/Yasin_Anwar" title="Yasin Anwar">Yasin Anwar</a> (State Bank of Pakistan), <a href="/wiki/Ignazio_Visco" title="Ignazio Visco">Ignazio Visco</a> (Bank of Italy), <a href="/wiki/Kim_Choongsoo" title="Kim Choongsoo">Kim Choongsoo</a> (Bank of Korea), <a href="/wiki/Zeti_Akhtar_Aziz" title="Zeti Akhtar Aziz">Zeti Akhtar Aziz</a> (Central Bank of Malaysia), <a href="/wiki/Pridiyathorn_Devakula" title="Pridiyathorn Devakula">Pridiyathorn Devakula</a> (Governor, Bank of Thailand, and former Minister of Finance), <a href="/wiki/Farouk_El_Okdah" title="Farouk El Okdah">Farouk El Okdah</a> (Central Bank of Egypt), and <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Prat_Gay" title="Alfonso Prat Gay" class="mw-redirect">Alfonso Prat Gay</a> (Central Bank of Argentina), as well as the director of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Economic_Council" title="United States National Economic Council">United States National Economic Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gene_Sperling" title="Gene Sperling">Gene Sperling</a>. Founders of technology companies include <a href="/wiki/Ralph_J._Roberts" title="Ralph J. Roberts">Ralph J. Roberts</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a>), <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a> (founder of <a href="/wiki/Paypal" title="Paypal" class="mw-redirect">Paypal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bosack" title="Leonard Bosack">Leonard Bosack</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Cisco" title="Cisco" class="mw-redirect">Cisco</a>), <a href="/wiki/David_J._Brown" title="David J. Brown">David Brown</a> (co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">Silicon Graphics</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Pincus" title="Mark Pincus">Mark Pincus</a> (founder of <a href="/wiki/Zynga" title="Zynga">Zynga</a>, the company behind <a href="/wiki/Farmville" title="Farmville" class="mw-redirect">Farmville</a>). Other notable businessmen and entrepreneurs who attended or graduated from the University of Pennsylvania include <a href="/wiki/William_S._Paley" title="William S. Paley">William S. Paley</a> (former president of <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>), <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>note 4<span>]</span></a></sup> (CEO of <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a>), <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump,_Jr." title="Donald Trump, Jr.">Donald Trump, Jr.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ivanka_Trump" title="Ivanka Trump">Ivanka Trump</a>, <a href="/wiki/Safra_Catz" title="Safra Catz" class="mw-redirect">Safra Catz</a> (President and CFO of <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a>), <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Lauder" title="Leonard Lauder">Leonard Lauder</a> (Chairman Emeritus of <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A9e_Lauder_Companies" title="Est&eacute;e Lauder Companies">Est&eacute;e Lauder Companies</a> and son of founder <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A9e_Lauder_(person)" title="Est&eacute;e Lauder (person)" class="mw-redirect">Est&eacute;e Lauder</a>), <a href="/wiki/Steven_A._Cohen" title="Steven A. Cohen">Steven A. Cohen</a> (founder of <a href="/wiki/SAC_Capital_Advisors" title="SAC Capital Advisors">SAC Capital Advisors</a>), <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kapito" title="Robert Kapito" class="mw-redirect">Robert Kapito</a> (president of <a href="/wiki/BlackRock" title="BlackRock">BlackRock</a>, the world's largest asset manager), and <a href="/wiki/P._Roy_Vagelos" title="P. Roy Vagelos">P. Roy Vagelos</a> (former president and CEO of multinational pharmaceutical company <a href="/wiki/Merck_%26_Co." title="Merck &amp; Co.">Merck &amp; Co.</a>).</p> 
     <p>Among other distinguished alumni are the current presidents of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drew_Gilpin_Faust" title="Drew Gilpin Faust">Drew Gilpin Faust</a>; the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Yudof" title="Mark Yudof">Mark Yudof</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morton_O._Schapiro" title="Morton O. Schapiro">Morton O. Schapiro</a>; poets <a href="/wiki/William_Augustus_Muhlenberg" title="William Augustus Muhlenberg">William Augustus Muhlenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Pound" title="Ezra Pound">Ezra Pound</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Carlos_Williams" title="William Carlos Williams">William Carlos Williams</a>, linguist and political theorist <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">Noam Chomsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starchitect" title="Starchitect">starchitect</a> <a href="/wiki/Louis_Kahn" title="Louis Kahn">Louis Kahn</a>, cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Charles_Addams" title="Charles Addams">Charles Addams</a>, theatrical producer <a href="/wiki/Harold_Prince" title="Harold Prince">Harold Prince</a>, counter-terrorism expert and author <a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Clarke" title="Richard A. Clarke">Richard A. Clarke</a>, pollster <a href="/wiki/Frank_Luntz" title="Frank Luntz">Frank Luntz</a>, attorney <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Allred" title="Gloria Allred">Gloria Allred</a>, journalist <a href="/wiki/Joe_Klein" title="Joe Klein">Joe Klein</a>, fashion designer <a href="/wiki/Tory_Burch" title="Tory Burch">Tory Burch</a>, recording artist <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, and football athlete and coach <a href="/wiki/John_Heisman" title="John Heisman">John Heisman</a>.</p> 
     <p>Within the ranks of Penn's most historic graduates are also eight signers of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> and nine signers of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution</a>. These include <a href="/wiki/George_Clymer" title="George Clymer">George Clymer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Hopkinson" title="Francis Hopkinson">Francis Hopkinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_McKean" title="Thomas McKean">Thomas McKean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morris_(financier)" title="Robert Morris (financier)">Robert Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Paca" title="William Paca">William Paca</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Ross_(delegate)" title="George Ross (delegate)">George Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Rush" title="Benjamin Rush">Benjamin Rush</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Wilson" title="James Wilson">James Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fitzsimons" title="Thomas Fitzsimons">Thomas Fitzsimons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jared_Ingersoll" title="Jared Ingersoll">Jared Ingersoll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rufus_King" title="Rufus King">Rufus King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mifflin" title="Thomas Mifflin">Thomas Mifflin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gouverneur_Morris" title="Gouverneur Morris">Gouverneur Morris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Williamson" title="Hugh Williamson">Hugh Williamson</a>.</p> 
     <p>In total, 28 Penn affiliates have won Nobel Prizes, of whom four are current faculty members and nine are alumni. Nine of the Nobel laureates have won the prize in the last decade. Penn also counts 115 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academies" title="United States National Academies">United States National Academies</a>, 79 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a> laureates, 108 <a href="/wiki/Sloan_Fellowship" title="Sloan Fellowship">Sloan Fellows</a>, 30 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>, and 170 <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowship" title="Guggenheim Fellowship">Guggenheim Fellowships</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>From 1930 to 1966 there were 54 documented <a href="/wiki/Rowbottom_(riot)" title="Rowbottom (riot)">Rowbottom riots</a>, a student tradition of rioting which included everything from car smashing to panty raids.<sup id="cite_ref-Rowbottom_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rowbottom-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> After 1966, there were five more instances of &quot;Rowbottoms&quot;, the latest occurring in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-Rowbottom_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rowbottom-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1965, Penn students learned that the University was sponsoring research projects for the United States' <a href="/wiki/United_States_biological_weapons_program" title="United States biological weapons program">chemical and biological weapons program</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CB_Controversy_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CB_Controversy-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Edward_S._Herman" title="Edward S. Herman">Herman</a> and Rutman, the revelation that &quot;CB Projects Spicerack and Summit were directly connected with U.S. military activities in Southeast Asia&quot;, caused students to petition Penn president <a href="/wiki/Gaylord_Harnwell" title="Gaylord Harnwell">Gaylord Harnwell</a> to halt the program, citing the project as being, &quot;immoral, inhuman, illegal, and unbefitting of an academic institution.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-CB_Controversy_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CB_Controversy-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Members of the faculty believed that an academic university should not be performing classified research and voted to re-examine the University agency which was responsible for the project on November 4, 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-CB_Controversy_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CB_Controversy-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1984, the Head Lab at the University of Pennsylvania was raided by members of the <a href="/wiki/Animal_Liberation_Front" title="Animal Liberation Front">Animal Liberation Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eco-Violence_report_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eco-Violence_report-114"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> 60 hours worth of video footage depicting animal cruelty was stolen from the lab.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethics_Report_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethics_Report-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The video footage was released to <a href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA" class="mw-redirect">PETA</a> who edited the tapes and created the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Unnecessary_Fuss" title="Unnecessary Fuss">Unnecessary Fuss</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethics_Report_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethics_Report-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result of an investigation called by the Office for Protection from Research Risks, the chief veterinarian was fired and the Head Lab was closed.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethics_Report_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethics_Report-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The school gained notoriety in 1993 for the <a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo_incident" title="Water buffalo incident">water buffalo incident</a> in which a student who told a noisy group of black students to &quot;shut up, you water buffalo&quot; was charged with violating the University's racial harassment policy.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pennsylvania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The University officially uses 1740 as its founding date and has since 1899. The ideas and intellectual inspiration for the academic institution stem from 1749, with a pamphlet published by Benjamin Franklin. When Franklin's institution was established, it inhabited a schoolhouse built in 1740 for another school, which never came to practical fruition. Penn archivist Mark Frazier Lloyd <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.upenn.edu/pennnews/current/node/2231">[1]</a> notes: ?In 1899, Penn?s Trustees adopted a resolution that established 1740 as the founding date, but good cases may be made for 1749, when Franklin first convened the Trustees, or 1751, when the first classes were taught at the affiliated secondary school for boys, Academy of Philadelphia, or 1755, when Penn obtained its collegiate charter to add a post-secondary institution, the College of Philadelphia.&quot; Princeton's library <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.princeton.edu/mudd/news/faq/topics/older.shtml">[2]</a> presents another, diplomatically phrased view.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Penn is the fourth-oldest using the founding dates claimed by each institution. Penn, <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia</a> originated within a few years of each other. Penn considered 1749 to be its founding date for more than a century, including at the centennial celebration in 1849. In 1895, elite universities in the United States convened in New York City as the &quot;Intercollegiate Commission&quot; at the invitation of <a href="/wiki/John_James_McCook_(lawyer)" title="John James McCook (lawyer)">John J. McCook</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> officer during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> and member of Princeton's board of trustees who chaired its Committee on Academic Dress. The primary purpose of the conference was to standardize American academic regalia, which was accomplished through the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Academic_regalia_in_the_United_States" title="Academic regalia in the United States">Intercollegiate Code on Academic Costume</a>. This formalized protocol included a provision that henceforth <a href="/wiki/Academic_procession" title="Academic procession">academic processions</a> would place visiting dignitaries and other officials in the order of their institution's founding dates. The following year, Penn's &quot;The Alumni Register&quot; magazine, published by the General Alumni Society, began a campaign to retroactively revise the university's founding date to 1740, in order to become older than Princeton, which had been chartered in 1746. Three years later in 1899, Penn's board of trustees acceded to this alumni initiative and officially changed its founding date from 1749 to 1740, affecting its rank in academic processions as well as the informal bragging rights that come with the age-based hierarchy in academia generally. See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.upenn.edu/gazette/0902/thomas.html">Building Penn's Brand</a> for more details on why Penn did this. <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> implicitly challenges this rationale, <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.princeton.edu/main/about/history/">[3]</a> also considering itself to be the nation's fourth oldest institution of higher learning. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.princeton.edu/main/about/history/american-revolution/">[4]</a> To further complicate the comparison, a University of Edinburgh-educated Presbyterian minister named <a href="/wiki/William_Tennent" title="William Tennent">William Tennent</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Tennent" title="Gilbert Tennent">Gilbert Tennent</a> operated a &quot;<a href="/wiki/Log_College" title="Log College">Log College</a>&quot; in Bucks County, Pennsylvania, from 1726 until 1746; some have suggested a connection between it and the College of New Jersey (later Princeton) because five members of Princeton's first Board of Trustees were affiliated with the Log College, including Gilbert Tennent, William Tennent, Jr., and Samuel Finley, the latter of whom later became President of Princeton. (All twelve members of Princeton's first Board of Trustees were leaders from the &quot;<a href="/wiki/The_Old_Side-New_Side_Controversy" title="The Old Side-New Side Controversy" class="mw-redirect">New Side</a>&quot; or &quot;<a href="/wiki/Old_and_New_Light" title="Old and New Light">New Light</a>&quot; wing of the Presbyterian Church in the New Jersey, New York and Pennsylvania area.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.princeton.edu/mudd/news/faq/topics/founders.shtml">[5]</a>) This antecedent relationship, if considered a formal lineage with institutional continuity, would justify pushing Princeton's founding date back to 1726, earlier than Penn's 1740. However, Princeton has not done so, and a Princeton historian says that &quot;the facts do not warrant&quot; such an interpretation. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://etcweb1.princeton.edu/CampusWWW/Companion/log_college.html">[6]</a> Columbia University also implicitly challenges Penn's use of either 1740 or 1749, as it claims to be the fifth oldest institution of higher learning in the United States (after Harvard, William &amp; Mary, Yale and Princeton), based upon its charter date of 1754 and Penn's charter date of 1755. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.columbia.edu/content/history.html">[7]</a> Academic histories of American higher education generally list Penn as fifth or sixth, after Princeton and immediately before or after Columbia. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://libx.bsu.edu/cdm4/document.php?CISOROOT=/ConspectusH&amp;CISOPTR=345&amp;REC=1">[8]</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://scholarship.rice.edu/bitstream/handle/1911/9120/article_RI234246.pdf?sequence=5">[9]</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ideals.illinois.edu/bitstream/handle/2142/3878/gslisoccasionalpv00000i00140.pdf?sequence=1">[10]</a> Even Penn's own account of its early history agrees that the Academy of Philadelphia did not add an institution of higher learning until 1755, but university officials continue to make it their practice to assert their fourth-oldest place in academic processions. Other American universities which began as colonial era secondary schools such as St. John's College in 1696 and the University of Delaware in 1743 choose to march based upon the date they became institutions of higher learning. According to sometime Penn History Professor Edgar Potts Cheyney, the University did indeed consider its founding date to be 1749 for almost a century. However, it was changed with good reason, and primarily due to a publication about the University issued by the U.S. Commissioner of Education. The year 1740 is the date of the establishment of the first educational trust that the University had taken upon itself. Cheyney states further that, &quot;it might be considered a lawyer's date; it is a familiar legal practice in considering the date of any institution to seek out the oldest trust it administers.&quot; He also points out that Harvard's founding date is *also* the year in which the Massachusetts General Court resolved to establish a fund in a year's time for a &quot;School or College&quot;. As well, Princeton claims its founding date as 1746--the date of its first charter. However, the exact words of the charter are unknown, the number and names of the trustees in the charter are unknown, and no known original is extant. With the exception of Columbia University, the majority of the American Colonial Colleges do not have clear-cut dates of foundation. (Edgar Potts Cheyney, &quot;History of the University of Pennsylvania: 1740-1940&quot;, Philadelphia: University of Pennsylvania Press, 1940: pp. 45-52.)</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1790, the first lecture on law was given by <a href="/wiki/James_Wilson" title="James Wilson">James Wilson</a>; however, a full time program was not offered until 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Buffett studied at Penn for 3 years before he transferred to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska" title="University of Nebraska" class="mw-redirect">University of Nebraska</a>.</span></li> 
      </ol> 
     </div>

     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of June 30, 2012. <span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nacubo.org/Documents/research/2012NCSEPublicTablesEndowmentMarketValuesFinalJanuary232013.pdf">&quot;U.S. and Canadian Institutions Listed by Fiscal Year 2012 Endowment Market Value and Percentage Change in Endowment Market Value from FY 2011 to FY 2012&quot;</a> (PDF). <i>2012 NACUBO-Commonfund Study of Endowments</i>.        <li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Edward_Potts_Cheyney" title="Edward Potts Cheyney">Cheyney, Edward Potts</a> (1940). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://repository.upenn.edu/penn_history/5/"><i>History of the University of Pennsylvania 1740?1940</i></a>. Philadelphia: University of Pennsylvania Press. pp.&nbsp;46?48<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved August 18, 2011. Cheyney was a Penn professor and alumnus from the class of 1883 who advocated the change in Penn's founding date in 1899 to appear older than both Princeton and Columbia. The explanation, &quot;It will have been noted that 1740 is the date of the creation of the earliest of the many educational trusts the University has taken upon itself,&quot; is Professor Cheyney's justification (pp. 47-48) for Penn retroactively changing its founding date, not language used by the Board of Trustees</span>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Pennsylvania&amp;rft.au=Cheyney%2C+Edward+Potts&amp;rft.aufirst=Edward+Potts&amp;rft.aulast=Cheyney&amp;rft.btitle=History+of+the+University+of+Pennsylvania+1740%E2%80%931940&amp;rft.date=1940&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Frepository.upenn.edu%2Fpenn_history%2F5%2F&amp;rft.pages=46%E2%80%9348&amp;rft.place=Philadelphia&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Pennsylvania+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>
